Kumta, ula file da ka political case No. 21 of 1925 pyrshah ia ki 12 shnong ka Sheila confedercy. Political Case No. 21 of 1925 Judgement The Sirdar of Nongbah (a British Village) complained that the people of the 12 village (Shelia Confederacy) are collecting revenue from the houses occupied by foreigners (ki dkhar) at the beach infront of his village Nongbah. I saw the place today and found it is part of Phali Bazar as regards which several officers e.g. Mr. Arbuthnott on 2 nd July. 1898 and Mr. Clarke on 2 nd October, 1909 passed orders saying that Phali Hat is an Old Hat and neither the Sirdar of Nongbah or anyone else has a right to collect revenue from it. Suba Sing, Headman of Nongwar, one of the 1 2 villages who acts as spokesman for the opposite party says that they have appointed year by year one of their men to look after the bazar and that this year they appointed U Sundon Kheifi to 171 look after the Bazar. Further, that each year occupying huts in Phali Bazar for expenses in connection with the bazar viz. making and repairing paths, bridges (14) and water channels (khriang) (7) in the rapids (ki khriang um) between Sheila Bazar and Ka Shyrten Stream. From my visit today to the Phali Bazar I can appreciate the work done by this concervancy Board and I see no reason to interfere with the people of the 12 villages collecting 'synfiiang’ for this purpose”. Camp Shelia, W.A. Cosgrave, 19.11.1925 Deputy Commissioner, K & J. Hills. Order of the Deputy Commissioner, Khasi and Jaintia Hills, dated the 5 th December, 1925 on the petition of U Jehari Sirdar of Nongbah dated the 25“’ November, 1925, in political case No. 21 of 1925. Inform Sirdar of Nongbah that I represent the Govern- ment in this matter and do no intend to levy house tax on these houses of foreigners at Phali Bazar and that if he makes any more trouble about this matter, he will be removed from his sirdarship and another man appointed in his place. W.A. Cosgrave, Deputy Commissioner, Khasf and Jaintia Hills, 5/12/25 Ha ka snem 1937 pat ki 8 shnong- Nongkroh, Tyrna, Ramdait.Nongbah, Tynrong, Nonglyngkin, Laitkynsew, 172 Mynteng-Nongriat da kaba ki ia syila napoh napoh bad ki Sheila ki pynTeng ia ka Hat Lba, hapoh llaka Shelia. Da kane ki Sheila ki thmu ban pyntroifl ia ka Hat Phali bad pynlong ia lade ki kynrad jong ka hat; namar ha ka durbar Phali ki Sheila kim i'oh kabu ban leh trai khlieh. Ba kumta, Ki Wadar ryngkat ki Sande 8 shnong ki phah ka ujor pyrshah sha ka Kashari U Commis- sioner, Surma Valley and Hills Division ha ka 24.3.1938, kaba ong kumne- Most respectfully shewith- (1) That by an Agreement dated the 17“* July, 1879 entered into in an open durbar at Phali Bazar between the 9 villages of the Shelia Confederacy on one part and the Wahadadars on the other part, it was inter alia settled that the two original and existing Hats namely Sheila and Phali should not be abolished and that the parties and their successors could not establish any new hat in the Confederacy, nor reopen the Hat Lyba which was abolished from the time of the Agreement and the parties would abide by the terms either by the Wahadadars or the people of the villages would be punished by expulsion and fines respectively. This Agreement recorded for the first time the unwritten law and usages of the people regarding commerce and trade and is regarded as a commercial code. Copy of the Agreement enclosed herewith at schedule 'A’. (2) That since the time of the aforesaid Agreement no attempt whtsoever has been made by the Wahadadars or villagers of the confederacy or even by the British villages outside the Confederacy to establish new Hats or reopen old defunct Hat Lyba. In 1936 however the spurious attempt on 173 part of the British Villages to open a new Hat within the confederacy territory was disallowed by K. Cantlie, Esqr., I.C.S. the then Deputy Commisioner and the Political Officer, Khasi and Jaintia Hills by an Order dated the 22 nd Oct. 1936. (Copy of order enclosed herewih as schedule ‘B’ & ‘C’. (3) That sometimes in the Summer of 1937 the Eight Villages outside the Confederacy applied to the Deputy Commisioner to open a new hat on the ground that they used the Phali Hat but have no share in its management, thereupon they were ordered by the Deputy Commisioner to name the place of their proposed Hat. But before obtaining the said order they already opened a hat in a place between the two existing hats of the Sheila Confederacy, i.e., within the Con- federacy. This new hat is meant to compete mainly with the orange business carried on by the people of the Confederacy on the one hand and on the other to compete and therby affect the general business of the two hats of the confederacy. (4) The Wahadadar protested to the Deputy Commi- sioner by a telegram sometime in the month of December against the encroachment of their rights by the said British Villages and pointed out to him the illegality of the actions of the said British Villages. Thereupon, on a record made upon inquiry by a Political Officer deputed for the same purpose by the Deputy Commisioner, the Deputy Commisioner stopped the said new hat. (5) Subsequently on the 28“’ of December, 1937, the Deputy Commisioner called all the parties concerned with the new hat at Cherra to enquire into the matter and passed an order to the effect that there were difficulties over giving a new 174 hat but if the 12 villages of the Confederacy agreed to the Phali durbar consisting of one person elected from each of the 23 villages this durbar to fix the rates of toll and method of management and distribution of money etc.then the agree- ment of 1 879 would be upheld and the new hat would be disal- lowed. The 12 villages had to report by the 5 m January, 1938 if they agreed to the increase in number. If they had not re- ported by then it would be taken that they did not agree. In the meantime the British Villages would continue to use the Phali Hat in the usual way. Their complain that they would get better prices by going a mile down nearer Sylhat were without foun- dation. If the 12 villages did not agree to the above arrange- ment then on certain condition a new hat would be allowed. That subsequently on the 21 s * of January, 1938, the Deputy Commisioner ordered a new hat to be established by the British Villages on certain conditions; the effect of which deprive the Shelia villages of any share in the management of the new hat though it is situated in their jurisdiction and that they must not use the Hat at all except that oranges which came from below the Phali Hat and above this hat could be exported through it, and further that the hat must be opened during the orange season. (Copy of order enclosed herewith as a schedule ‘C’ and ‘D’, being aggrieved by the said order of the Deputy commisioner your petitioners beg to prefer this petition of appeal on the following amongst other- Grounds (1 ) For that the Deputy Commissioner’s orders are irregu- lar and illegal. 175 (2) For that there was no evidence to the effect that new state of things have risen which show that any grave injustice had been done to the villages outside the con- federacy which warranted the abolision or the agree- ment of 17 th July, 1879, which cannot be abolished with- out the consent of the people. (3) For that the attempt to create a new durbar consisting of representatives of 23 villages is an innovation and indirect violation of the treaty rights of the people of the confederacy as well as the Wahadadars. (4) For that instead of helping the 8 villages and preventing any further troubles as contemplated by the learned Deputy Commission the orders by its terms only will aggravate the conditions and produce more troubles and subsequently breach of the peace. (5) For that the new Hat will become a serious menace to the economic prosperity of the villages of the confed- eracy by its competition and paralyse the trade of the place specially in orange. (6) For that the learned Deputy Commisioner erred in law in holding that the British Villages can have any right in the management or establish a hat outside their own jurisdiction i.e within the jurisdiction of the Confederacy. (7) For that the learned Deputy Commisioner ought to have been guided by the precedent set forth in the order of the former Deputy Commisioner dated 22 nd of October, 1936 and ought to have held that the 8 villages suffer no such trouble that they ought to have a new hat. 176 (8) For that the order of the learned Deputy Commisioner is indirect violation of the unwritten law of the people concern embodied in the agreement of 1879, and the facts of the case did not warrant any drastic abolition of the status quo of the confederacy. (9) For that the learned Deputy Commisioner erred in law in holding that those who use a hat can have a right and share in management of the hat simply because they use the hat. (10) For that the learned Deputy Commisioner has failed to realise the true facts of the case and appears to have leaned towards partiality by allowing the hat to be estab- lished by outsiders in the Confederacy to use the hat or to have a share in the management of the hat situated in their own territory, threby encouraging the 8 villages (British villages) inpersuing a policy of trespass. (11) That the learned Deputy Commidioner ought not to have abolished the Agreement of 1 897 but ought to have con- tinued the policy which have obtained with regard to the matters in disputes since over half a century and not abolish the personal law and customs without any strong foundation. (12) For that the Learned Deputy Comisioner had failed to recognise the fact that the Agreement of 1 879 is of vital importance to the concerned as it regulates their economic existence. The petitioners therefore pray that your honour may be pleased to admit this appeal after calling for the records and hearing your petitioners’ lawyers set aside the Order of the 177 Deputy Commisioner passed on the 28* December, 1937 and 21*' January, 1938 respectively and upheld the Agreement of 17"’ July, 1879 and abolish the new hat established in their Confederacy territory by the 8 villages (British Villages) and to issue an injunction on the villagers of the 8 villages from continuing the hat till the disposal of the appeal petition and to pass such further order or orders as your honour may dim fit and proper. And your petitiners an on duty bound shall ever pray. Humble appelants, B. Iso Roy U Orju Dated Shillong, U Jebuni The 24 th March, 1938 Horinson Buhroy Wahadadars of the Shelia Confederacy. Halor ka jingkwah U Deputy Commisioner ban tip la ki 12 shnong jong ka Shelia Confederacy ki mon ne em ban shah ia ki 8 shnong jong ki Sirdar (British Villages) ban ia don kti lang ha ka jingpyni'aid ia ka Hat Phali bad ba u kwah ban Toh da ka jingthoh na ki ha ne shuwa ka 5 tarik January, 1938: khnang ba un sngewthuh la un shah ne em ia kitei ki 8 shnong ban plie hat thymmai. Ki Wahadadar ha ka 2 tarik, Janu- ary, 1938 ki ai kane ka report- Ha U Deputy Commisioner, Khasi and Jaintia Hills, Shillong. Ka Report ki Wahadadar ka Sheila Confederacy lem bad ki Headmen bad ki Nongmihkhmat jong ki 12 shnong kiba long ki trai ka Hat Phali ia ka jingkwah U Deputy Commis- 178 sioner ba ula ong ha Sohra ha ka dt. 28" December, 1937 ban ia long trai lang bad ki shnong Sirdar ha ka jingpynVaid ia ka Hat Phali ia kaba ki 12 shnong ki long ki trai naduh hyndai hynthai. Sahep badonburom, Ngi ki Wadar lem bad ki Headmen bad ki Rangbah nongmihkhmat jong ki 1 2 shnong, ngi la ia pyrkhat bniah ha ka durbar pyllun ia ka jingong ka burom jongphi ba ki shnong Sirdar kin ia long trai noh ryngkat bad ngi ia ka hat Phali, bad ngi kyrpad rit ban ong kumne harum- (1) Ba ki 12 shnong kirn lah satia ban pynduh noh ia la ka hok ka jinglongtrai kynti ia ka Hat Phali, ia kaba kila don naduh ba la seng ia ka la bun spah snem mynta bad ia kaba la pynskhem da ki rai ki Deputy Commissioner bad ki Nongsynshar ba ka khih top-shi-top naduh U Col. Raban ha ka 4 tarik March, 1937 bad U Col. H. Kinson, Agent to the Gover- nor General NEF ha ka 29 tarik February, 1872 haduh U Sahab K. Cantlee, Deputy Commissioner ha ka dt. 22 tarik Octo- ber, 1936. (2) Ba U Sahep K. Cantlee, D.C. ha ka hukum jong u dt. 22 tarik, October, 1936, u la pynbeit ia ka jingpynVaid ia ka hat Phali bad ia kata ka jingpynbeit jong U Sahep, ki shnong Sirdar kumjuh lem ki 12 shnong kila sngewhun bad kohnguh. Ka durbar Hat Phali kaba mihkhmat ia ki 12 shnong kala pynTaid ia ka hat Phali thik kat kata ka hukum. U soh u pai na ki shnong Sirdar ula poi ha hat Phali mynta ka snem bad ha katei ka snem kumjuh kumba poi na 12 shnong ha ka jingsuk jingsaifl khlem don jingud ne jingduh jinglutksan ne jingphah leh beifi mano 179 mano. Katba ngi ki Wadar bad ka Durbar Hat Phali ngi lah bna Vohi bad ban tip. Ngim lah sngewthuh namar kata, ki don daw al'u ba ki shong durbar ban pynkhih thma mynta pat tang shisnem tarn hadien kata ka hukum. (3) Ba kumba long ha ki hat baroh hajan pud ri dkhar ki don ki dkhar bad ki Khasi na kiba bun ki hima bad ki shnong ki bym long trai ia ki hat; hynrei kiba wanlam ne wan thied mar bad ha kata ka rukom kila pynheh pynkhraw ia ki hat. Kumta ruh ka long ka Hat Phali jongngi. Baroh bad dkhar bad khasi ki hun ha ka jingpyni'aid ia ka Hat Phlai lait noh na ki shnong Sirdar. Ngi kyrpad ia ka burom jongphi ban sneng ia ki kum ki kpa ia la ki khun ba kin ym mlien shuh ban shu pynshitom kai ia phi ki Sorkar bad ia ngi ki 1 2 shnong da kaba thaw kum kine khlem daw ei ei ruh em. (4) Ba ka Hat Phali bad Hat sheila ki long ki thied snam bah ha kiba shong ka jingTap bad ka jingim ka Shelia Confed- eracy. Nangta ngi kyrpad rit ban buh ha khmat ka burom basbun jongphi ba ha ka liang ka Sheila Confederacy bad na ka liang ka sorkar, phi kiba kitkhia na ka bynta ka jingbha ki Hima Khasi jongngi: ym bit ban don hangno hangno ha wah Sheila hapoh ka Shelia Confederacy kawei pat ka Hat ka ban long Trai bad pyni'aid da ka bor kaba nabar ka Confederacy. Naduh kane ka porym don mokotduma shuh halor ka Hat Phali.
